      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Bulgarian Air Force
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">
        Bulgarian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="bg" xml:lang="bg">
        Военновъздушни сили
       </span>
       ) is one of the three branches of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Bulgaria" title="Military of Bulgaria">
        Military of Bulgaria
       </a>
       , the other two being the
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Navy" title="Bulgarian Navy">
        Bulgarian Navy
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulgarian_land_forces" title="Bulgarian land forces">
        Bulgarian land forces
       </a>
       . Its mission is to guard and protect the sovereignty of
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">
        Bulgarian
       </a>
       airspace, to provide aerial support and to assist the Land Forces in case of war. The Bulgarian Air Force is one of the oldest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_forces" title="Air forces">
        air forces
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       and the world. In recent times it has been actively taking part in numerous
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       missions and
       <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">
        exercises
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">
        Europe
       </a>
       . The current commanding officer of the Bulgarian Air Force is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_General" title="Major General">
        Major General
       </a>
       Constantin Popov.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          </li>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">
        Early years
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masl.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="187" data-file-width="401" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/04/Masl.jpg/220px-Masl.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/04/Masl.jpg/330px-Masl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/0/04/Masl.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masl.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Boris Maslennikov's airplane in flight, Sofia 1910
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bulgarian Air Force dates back to the end of the 19th century. In 1892 at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plovdiv_International_Fair" title="Plovdiv International Fair">
        Plovdiv International Fair
       </a>
       two lieutenants of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Army" title="Bulgarian Army">
        Bulgarian Army
       </a>
       flew in the ‘La France’
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balloon_(aircraft)" title="Balloon (aircraft)">
        balloon
       </a>
       of the Frenchman
       <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Godard" title="Eugène Godard">
        Godard
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Later, inspired by the flight, they succeeded to convince the General Staff that the Bulgarian Army should build a balloon force. The Imperial Aviation School in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" title="St. Petersburg">
        St. Petersburg
       </a>
       enrolled Lieutenant Vasil Zlatarov as a student, following numerous refusals from military schools around Europe to teach Bulgarian officers to use airships. On 20 April 1906 "Vazduhoplavatelno Otdelenie" (roughly translated as Aviation Squad) was created to operate observation balloons for the army, initially being a part of Railway Battalion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After graduation Lt. Zlatarov was appointed its first commander. After operating small balloons, in 1911 a bigger Godard balloon was bought, and in 1912 the first balloon Sofia-1 was constructed in Bulgaria, of materials bought from
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1910 a Russian aircraft engineer, Boris Maslennikov, was invited to
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">
        Bulgaria
       </a>
       , where he presented his airplane, a modification of the French
       <a href="/wiki/Farman_III" title="Farman III">
        Farman III
       </a>
       . Following his demonstration, assisted by Vasil Zlatarov over the hippodrome in
       <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">
        Sofia
       </a>
       , the Bulgarian Government decided to acquire airplanes for The Aviation Corps. In early 1912 thirteen army officers were sent abroad for training as pilots and orders were placed for five French, British and German airplanes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The officers sent to France completed their training first and returned to Bulgaria in July 1912. The same year Bulgaria received its first airplane –
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bleriot_XXI" title="Bleriot XXI">
        Bleriot XXI
       </a>
       with which on 13 August 1912 Simeon Petrov flew to become the first Bulgarian to pilot an airplane over Bulgaria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_and_Second_Balkan_Wars">
        First and Second Balkan Wars
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First and Second Balkan Wars">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="600" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg/220px-Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg/330px-Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg/440px-Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bleriot_XI_-_Simeon_Petrov.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Simon_Petrov" title="Simon Petrov">
          Simon Petrov
         </a>
         in a Bleriot XI 1912
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the outbreak of the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">
        First Balkan War
       </a>
       , Bulgarian pilots still abroad hastily procured aircraft to be shipped home after them and foreign volunteer pilots converged from all over Europe in Bulgaria.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aeroflight.co.uk_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aeroflight.co.uk-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the front lines had stabilized, an Aeroplane Platoon was established at a new airfield close to the fighting.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aeroflight.co.uk_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aeroflight.co.uk-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Intelligence about the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_army" title="Turkish army">
        Turkish army
       </a>
       strength and dispositions in the
       <a href="/wiki/Edirne" title="Edirne">
        Edirne
       </a>
       was required, and on
       <a href="/wiki/1912_in_aviation" title="1912 in aviation">
        16 October 1912
       </a>
       , two aviators performed a reconnaissance flight over the city in an
       <a href="/wiki/Farman_III" title="Farman III">
        Albatros FIII
       </a>
       biplane, dropping also two bombs, which was not only the first military mission performed by a Bulgarian aircraft, but also the first combat use of an aircraft in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Later that month the Bulgarian Aviation Corps was expanded to three Aeroplane Platoons. Foreign volunteers began flying operational sorties alongside Bulgarian pilots and carried out
       <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance" title="Reconnaissance">
        reconnaissance
       </a>
       , leaflet-dropping and bombing missions. During the war at least three aircraft were shot down. Considerable help was received from the Russians in terms of aircraft, maintenance and training. Due to low aircraft serviceability and frequent accidents, the number of missions flown was relatively low. Despite that, the Bulgarian airmen and their foreign helpers were able to gather enough intelligence for the Army General Staff to use in the capture of the city. Although inflicting little physical damage, the bombs had a devastating effect on the defending Turkish garrison's morale and played a crucial part in the fall of the city, which was until then considered nearly impregnable.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       During the First Balkan War Bulgarian aviation undertook 70 combat sorties, including 11 bombing raids, during the Second Balkan War it undertook 6 sorties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       All in all, during both wars, there were over 230 aircraft sorties, including non-combat.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The aircraft used were
       <a href="/wiki/Bl%C3%A9riot_XI" title="Blériot XI">
        Blériot XI
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bl%C3%A9riot_XXI" title="Blériot XXI">
        XXI
       </a>
       , Voisin, Sommer, Albatros FIII, Bristol,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Farman_VII&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Farman VII (page does not exist)">
        Farman VII
       </a>
       and Nieuport IV.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bulg1_1-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-bulg1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="World_War_I_.281914.E2.80.931918.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I_(1914–1918)">
        World War I (1914–1918)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: World War I (1914–1918)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Army_air_action">
        Army air action
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Army air action">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg/160px-Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg/240px-Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg/320px-Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg.png 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cross-Pattee-Heraldry.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Insignia from 1915 to 1918
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria" title="Kingdom of Bulgaria">
        Kingdom of Bulgaria
       </a>
       entered
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       as an ally of the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">
        Central Powers
       </a>
       on October 4, 1915. The Aeroplane Section of the Bulgarian Army was deployed to
       <a href="/wiki/Kumanovo" title="Kumanovo">
        Kumanovo
       </a>
       Airfield in support of advancing Bulgarian forces, but bad weather initially prevented any flying. Until then they had completed 11 combat sorties from an airfield in
       <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">
        Sofia
       </a>
       (now the central railway station).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       As the frontline advanced, the unit re-deployed to airfields near Belitsa and
       <a href="/wiki/Xanthi" title="Xanthi">
        Xanthi
       </a>
       , in modern
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       . Newly acquired German
       <a href="/wiki/LVG" title="LVG">
        LVG
       </a>
       aircraft were hastily pressed into action.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Two more airfields were constructed near Udovo and Levunovo. The
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">
        Allies
       </a>
       began flying reconnaissance and bomber sorties against Bulgarian units on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_front_(World_War_I)" title="Macedonian front (World War I)">
        Southern Balkan Front
       </a>
       . Throughout World War I Bulgarian military aviation experienced a steady increase in both numbers and quality of aircraft; however, they remained inferior to those flown by the Allies, especially the British and French. The First Aeroplane Section (the country's only aircraft unit) was attached to the Second Bulgarian Army. It flew 255 sorties compared to 397 flown by the four squadrons of the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">
        Entente
       </a>
       it opposed, and operated the following types:
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        12
        <a href="/wiki/LVG" title="LVG">
         LVG
        </a>
        B.II – reconnaissance aircraft, the first group of six arriving in November 1915. Those two seaters were also used as fighters by the Bulgarians, as dedicated "scouts" were not available.
       </li>
       <li>
        13 Otto C.I – a twin-tailed pusher bomber. The first Otto in arrived in May 1916.
       </li>
       <li>
        18
        <a href="/wiki/Albatros_C.III" title="Albatros C.III">
         Albatros C.III
        </a>
        – reconnaissance aircraft, also used as trainers. First delivery in August 1916.
       </li>
       <li>
        12
        <a href="/wiki/DFW_C.V" title="DFW C.V">
         DFW C.V
        </a>
        – reconnaissance aircraft, first arriving in August 1917.
       </li>
       <li>
        6 Roland D.II fighters. During July 1917 the first of these arrived with the Section.
       </li>
       <li>
        6 Roland D.III fighters, the first arriving at the end of 1917.
       </li>
       <li>
        3
        <a href="/wiki/Fokker_E.III" title="Fokker E.III">
         Fokker E.III
        </a>
        fighters, first of these delivered in the spring of 1916.
       </li>
       <li>
        8
        <a href="/wiki/Fokker_D.VII" title="Fokker D.VII">
         Fokker D.VII
        </a>
        – the best fighter used by Bulgaria in World War I. Delivery took place in September 1918 and they saw no action. 7 were scrapped in accordance with the peace treaty. The 8th flew as a two-seater after the war.
       </li>
       <li>
        2
        <a href="/wiki/Albatros_C.I" title="Albatros C.I">
         Albatros C.I
        </a>
        . These were ordered by the Ottoman Empire before Bulgaria entered the war. During early 1915 a couple landed on then neutral Bulgarian territory after a navigational error, and they were seized.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In addition, the Bulgarian Navy used the following airplanes:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        8 Friedrichshafen FF-33 floatplane bombers, starting in 1916
       </li>
       <li>
        2 Rumpler 6B1 floatplane fighters, starting in 1916
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       A number of Bulgarian pilots flew with German air units at the
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">
        Western Front
       </a>
       and at Xanthi. They operated several types, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Albatros_D.III" title="Albatros D.III">
        Albatros D.III
       </a>
       and Halberstadt, which would later mistakenly be listed on the Bulgarian inventory by some sources.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Captured_Allied_aircraft">
        Captured Allied aircraft
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Captured Allied aircraft">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="1024" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg/220px-Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg/330px-Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg/440px-Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armstrong-Whitworth_FK3_captured.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bulgarian airmen in captured British
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armstrong_Whitworth_FK.3" title="Armstrong Whitworth FK.3">
          Armstrong Whitworth FK.3
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 30 September 1916 a French
       <a href="/wiki/Farman_F.40" title="Farman F.40">
        Farman F.40
       </a>
       bomber of Escadrille 384 was tasked with attacking the Bulgarian capital,
       <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">
        Sofia
       </a>
       . Two Bulgarian
       <a href="/wiki/Fokker_E.III" title="Fokker E.III">
        Fokker E.IIIs
       </a>
       were positioned south of Sofia to intercept the intruder, while a flight of three armed Albatros C.III two-seat trainers covered the center of the city as backup. The bomber successfully dropped its bombs over Sofia while escaping anti-aircraft fire but, while departing, was attacked by the Bulgarian Fokkers which brought the Farman down with a dead engine.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another Allied aircraft, a
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        British
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Armstrong_Whitworth_F.K.3" title="Armstrong Whitworth F.K.3">
        Armstrong Whitworth F.K.3
       </a>
       , was captured by Bulgarian troops on 12 February 1917 after engine problems forced it to land. Both it and the crew were captured. It would receive Bulgarian insignia and be used to bomb Allied positions at night. Four such sorties were flown before being shot down on 23 May 1918.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nieuport_24bis" title="Nieuport 24bis">
        Nieuport 24bis
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Nieuport_27" title="Nieuport 27">
        Nieuport 27
       </a>
       were also captured. Lieutenant Vladimir Balan, a Bulgarian fighter pilot who had been flying with a German Jasta on the Western Front, was flying one of the Nieuports when he shot down the squadron leader of
       <a href="/wiki/No._17_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 17 Squadron RAF">
        No. 17 Squadron RAF
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_air_action">
        Naval air action
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Naval air action">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Bulgarian naval aviators also played an important role in the air war. In 1912
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petty-Officer" title="Petty-Officer">
        Petty-Officers
       </a>
       Lyapchev and Mikhailov were sent, along with other officers and seamen, to the German naval aviation forming facilities for training. Another group of naval personnel followed in the beginning of the First World War. Training was held at List, Nordenhai and Kiel. In November 1915 a
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seaplane_station&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seaplane station (page does not exist)">
        seaplane station
       </a>
       under German control was established near
       <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">
        Varna
       </a>
       , initially operating four Friedrichshafen FF-33 bombers and a Rumpler 6B1 fighter. Later, at the coast of the Varna Lake, a second
       <a href="/wiki/Seaplane" title="Seaplane">
        seaplane
       </a>
       station was built (this one under Bulgarian control), operating the same inventory. Near
       <a href="/wiki/Sozopol" title="Sozopol">
        Sozopol
       </a>
       a forward fuel and ammunition replenishment base was established in support of patrol flights over the southern Bulgarian coastline. At the end of 1917 the German station was transferred to the Bulgarian Navy. At the time of the armistice the Bulgarian fleet air arm comprised two seaplane stations, a forward replenishment base, three hangars, three workshops, ammunition warehouses and 10 seaplanes. After the cease-fire the machines were used for mine reconnaissance. At the end of 1919 they are transported by train to
       <a href="/wiki/Bozhurishte" title="Bozhurishte">
        Bozhurishte
       </a>
       Airfield to be scrapped along with the army aviation inventory.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bulgarian balloon observers also took part in the war. They were most active on the
       <a href="/wiki/Dobruja" title="Dobruja">
        Dobrudzha
       </a>
       Front, where aircraft activities were scarce (a German bomber squadron, flying missions against
       <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">
        Bucharest
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constan%C5%A3a" title="Constanţa">
        Constanţaine
       </a>
       : "Gotha" bombers accounted for the most flights). Near the Bulgarian city of
       <a href="/wiki/Yambol" title="Yambol">
        Yambol
       </a>
       an
       <a href="/wiki/Airship_hangar" title="Airship hangar">
        airship hangar
       </a>
       was constructed to house German airships. The airship Schütte-Lanz SL 10 was the first to use it. According to documents of the time it was assigned to the Bulgarian Army, but was actually under German control. It was lost during a flight over the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">
        Black Sea
       </a>
       in July 1916. In August 1916 the LZ 101 replaced it. After performing raids on targets in Romania and Greece it returned to Germany in August 1917. In November 1917 the naval airship
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zeppelin_LZ104" title="Zeppelin LZ104">
        L 59
       </a>
       arrived. That airship flew a series of remarkable missions, such as an attempted resupply of the garrison in the colony
       <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">
        German East Africa
       </a>
       and the bombing of
       <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">
        Naples
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Port_Said" title="Port Said">
        Port Said
       </a>
       . During a mission against the British naval base in
       <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
        Malta
       </a>
       , a lightning strike over the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean Sea
       </a>
       set it alight and completely destroyed it. All hands were lost.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fallschirmjaeger_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fallschirmjaeger-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Destruction_and_survival_under_the_peace_treaty_.281919.E2.80.931936.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Destruction_and_survival_under_the_peace_treaty_(1919–1936)">
        Destruction and survival under the peace treaty (1919–1936)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Destruction and survival under the peace treaty (1919–1936)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 4 October 1918 the Bulgarian Tsar issued a Royal Act of Demobilization. This resulted in military aviation being converted to its peace-time structure.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Aeroplane group, based in Bozhurishte comprised the following:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Two aeroplane companies
       </li>
       <li>
        An aeroplane school
       </li>
       <li>
        An aeroplane atelliér
       </li>
       <li>
        An aeroplane depot
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The Chaika Naval Seaplane station at Varna was under Naval command.
      </p>
      <p>
       On November 27, 1919 the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Neuilly-sur-Seine" title="Treaty of Neuilly-sur-Seine">
        Treaty of Neuilly-sur-Seine
       </a>
       was signed. In accordance with the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">
        treaty
       </a>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria" title="Kingdom of Bulgaria">
        Kingdom of Bulgaria
       </a>
       was banned from operating
       <a href="/wiki/Military_aircraft" title="Military aircraft">
        military aircraft
       </a>
       under any form for the next 20 years. For that reason all Bulgarian airplanes, balloons, aviation equipment, weaponry and ammunition were to be destroyed under Allied control. Under the terms of the treaty any aircraft procured for civilian purposes had to be bought from the countries on the winning side. The combined engine power for any airplane (including multi-engined ones) was not to exceed 180 hp. In addition, the Bulgarian airspace was to be controlled by the allies and used according to the victorious countries' interests.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In accordance with the treaty during 1920 no less than 70
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airplanes" title="Airplanes">
        airplanes
       </a>
       , 110
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Aviation_engines&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Aviation engines (page does not exist)">
        aviation engines
       </a>
       , 3 air
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balloons" title="Balloons">
        balloons
       </a>
       , 76
       <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">
        aviation
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machine_guns" title="Machine guns">
        machine guns
       </a>
       , a number of photographic
       <a href="/wiki/Camera" title="Camera">
        cameras
       </a>
       and other aviation equipment were destroyed at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_airfield" title="Military airfield">
        military airfield
       </a>
       of Bozhurishte. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaplanes" title="Seaplanes">
        seaplanes
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Navy" title="Bulgarian Navy">
        Bulgarian Navy
       </a>
       were delivered by train to the same airfield and scrapped soon after that.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dar10.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="750" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dar10.jpg/220px-Dar10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dar10.jpg/330px-Dar10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dar10.jpg/440px-Dar10.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dar10.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Bulgarian-manufactured
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DAR-10" title="DAR-10">
          DAR-10
         </a>
         training plane. DAR produced small numbers of locally designed aircraft
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Due to the devotion of the Air Troops personnel and the help of the population of the surrounding villages, several aircraft were hidden, thus evading Allied inspection following destruction. Seven DFW C.V, Albatros C.III and a single Fokker D.VII were among the survivors. In addition, at least ten aviation engines (Benz-IV and Mercedes-III) were also saved.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bulgarian government tried to get around the ban for military flight activity by establishing a Gendarmery Aeroplane Section in 1919. Since the Gendarmery was at that time a service under the Ministry of War, the creation of the unit was met by fierce opposition by the Allied commission. This almost resulted in the destruction of the whole
       <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport" title="Sofia Airport">
        Vrazhdebna Airfield
       </a>
       , but the disbandment of the unit prevented this from happening.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       An Aeroflight Section under the Ministry of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railway" title="Railway">
        Railways
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Postal_Service" title="Postal Service">
        Postal Service
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telegraph" title="Telegraph">
        Telegraph
       </a>
       was created in 1920. Bulgarian aviation personnel assembled two airplanes from hidden spares and parts, salvaged from the destroyed military airplanes. The two aircraft, known as "the mixed planes", recorded about 1000 flight hours altogether. The sole remaining Bulgarian Fokker D.VII was disguised as a two-seater, thus being classified as a trainer and returning to active service.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 5 July 1923 Bulgaria ratified the International Civil Aviation Treaty. From that moment on its air vehicles would carry a registration in the form B-B??? (the latter three signs being a combination of capital letters). In 1923 the first group of cadets, called "student-flyers" entered the Flying school at Vrazhdebna AF.
      </p>
      <p>
       The following year (1924) the first new airplanes were acquired. Those were machines of the
       <a href="/wiki/Potez" title="Potez">
        Potez
       </a>
       VIII,
       <a href="/wiki/Caudron_C.59" title="Caudron C.59">
        Caudron C.59
       </a>
       , Henriot XD.14, Bristol 29 Tourer types;
       <a href="/wiki/Avro" title="Avro">
        Avro
       </a>
       522 seaplanes were also procured. During the same year the Bulgarian airplane construction specialist Atanas Grigorov (who obtained his qualification at the "Albatroswerke – Berlin") assembled his seaplane, called "Grigorov-1". The aircraft made several test-flights, recording excellent characteristics, but was damaged beyond repair by a storm in the hangar where it was stationed. Also in 1924 the Aeroplane Section was expanded to an Aeroflight Directorate still under the Ministry of Railways, Postal Service and Telegraph.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       1925 saw the Potez XVII,
       <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Primary_Trainer" title="Bristol Primary Trainer">
        Bristol Lucifer
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Alenia_Aermacchi" title="Alenia Aermacchi">
        Macchi
       </a>
       2000/18 flying boats boosting the country's aircraft inventory. The Bulgarian government invited a group of German aircraft engineers, headed by the constructor Herr Hermann Winter to help establish an aviation factory. Named The State's Aeroconstruction Atelliér (more popular as DAR-Bozhurishte) the factory was initially managed by the first Bulgarian pilot to achieve an aerial victory – Mr. Marko Parvanov. The first aircraft types, produced by the plant were the "Uzounov-1" (an indigenous variant of the wartime German DFW C.V) and the DAR-2 (indigenous variant of the German
       <a href="/wiki/Albatros_C.III" title="Albatros C.III">
        Albatros C.III
       </a>
       of the same era). Both types well-known and loved by the personnel of the former Air Troops and with Bulgarian combat service experience. A new type – the DAR-1 – was also in a phase of development.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stele-Plovdiv.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1005" data-file-width="654" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Stele-Plovdiv.jpg/220px-Stele-Plovdiv.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Stele-Plovdiv.jpg/330px-Stele-Plovdiv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Stele-Plovdiv.jpg/440px-Stele-Plovdiv.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stele-Plovdiv.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         One of the eagles that decorated the entrance of
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bozhurishte_Air_Base&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bozhurishte Air Base (page does not exist)">
          Bozhurishte Air Base
         </a>
         in the 1930s and 1940s, now preserved at the
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plovdiv_Museum_of_Aviation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plovdiv Museum of Aviation (page does not exist)">
          Plovdiv Museum of Aviation
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the course of 1926 the Airplane School was moved to the geographical center of the country. The town of
       <a href="/wiki/Kazanlak" title="Kazanlak">
        Kazanlak
       </a>
       was well suited, for it stayed away from the Allied Control Commission. The
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovak
       </a>
       "AERO-Praha" company also built an aircraft factory near that city, but its models were not up to the requirements of the Bulgarian authorities. After an unsuccessful switch to automotive production, the plant was finally sold to the Italian
       <a href="/wiki/Caproni" title="Caproni">
        Caproni
       </a>
       company. The factory became popular as "Balgarski Kaproni" or "Bulgarian Caproni". The first examples of the very successful DAR-1 were produced and entered service with the Aeroflight Directorate during 1926.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1927 structure of the Directorate was the following:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        A fighter yato,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-4">
          [NOTE 1]
         </a>
        </sup>
        flying the DAR-1s
       </li>
       <li>
        A bomber yato, flying the DAR-"Uzounov-1" and DAR-2
       </li>
       <li>
        A recon yato, flying the Potez XVIIs
       </li>
       <li>
        A seaplane yato, flying the Avro 522 floatplanes and the Macchi 2000/18 flying boats
       </li>
       <li>
        An aeroplane school, flying the Caudron C-59, the Henriot XD.14 and the Šmolnik Š.18
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In 1928 the Ministry of War started the ambitious 10-year program for development of the military aviation (still banned by the peace treaty). According to the plan the following structure had to be achieved:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        4 army fighter orlyaks,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-5">
          [NOTE 2]
         </a>
        </sup>
        each made of two yatos, or overall 8 yatos flying 96 fighter planes
       </li>
       <li>
        4 army recon orlyaks, each made of two yatos, or overall 8 yatos flying 96 recon planes
       </li>
       <li>
        18 divisionary recon yatos, basically air support aviation, each flying 12 planes or 216 planes altogether
       </li>
       <li>
        Strike Aviation Brigade with:
        <ul>
         <li>
          Fighter Orlyak of 48 machines
         </li>
         <li>
          Bomber Orlyak of 36 machines
         </li>
         <li>
          Recon Orlyak of 2 machines
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Maritime Orlyak
        <ul>
         <li>
          2 seaplane fighter yatos, flying 24 fighters
         </li>
         <li>
          2 seaplane bomber yatos, flying 18 bombers
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In 1931 Bulgaria signed the Warsaw Treaty, concerning international civil air activities and the country was assigned the new civil registration – LZ-??? (the latter three signs being a combination of capital letters). In 1933 the Bulgarian Council of Ministers approved the following wartime order of battle of the aviation:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        a mixed orlyak of:
        <ul>
         <li>
          a fighter yato
         </li>
         <li>
          a bomber yato
         </li>
         <li>
          a recon yato
         </li>
         <li>
          a liaison and photographic survey yato
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        a maritime yato
       </li>
       <li>
        a training orlyak
       </li>
       <li>
        a Pilot School at Kazanlak airfield
       </li>
       <li>
        a balloon company (which was never actually created, as the balloon was considered obsolete for military purposes at the time).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Bulgaria started acquiring German, Czechoslovak and Polish airplanes.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1934 the Aviation Regiment was renamed His Majesty's Air Troops, comprising a headquarters, with two army orlyaks (based at
       <a href="/wiki/Bozhurishte" title="Bozhurishte">
        Bozhurishte
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">
        Plovdiv
       </a>
       airfields), a training orlyak (in
       <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">
        Plovdiv
       </a>
       ), a maritime yato (at NAS Chaika, Varna) and additional operational support units. Chief of the HMAT became Colonel Ivan Mikhailov with Lieutenant-Colonel Georgi Vasilev appointed as his Deputy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fallschirmjaeger_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Fallschirmjaeger-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Years_of_Rebirth_.281937.E2.80.931939.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Years_of_Rebirth_(1937–1939)">
        Years of Rebirth (1937–1939)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Years of Rebirth (1937–1939)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1937-1941).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281937-1941%29.svg/160px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281937-1941%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281937-1941%29.svg/240px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281937-1941%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281937-1941%29.svg/320px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281937-1941%29.svg.png 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1937-1941).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Insignia from 1937 to 1941, also the
         <a href="/wiki/Orders,_decorations,_and_medals_of_Bulgaria" title="Orders, decorations, and medals of Bulgaria">
          Medal of Bravery
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The first combat aircraft that entered service in the reestablished air force in 1937 were 12 Arado Ar.65 fighters, 12 Heinkel He.51 fighters, 12 Dornier Do.11 bombers and 12 Heinkel He.45B recon planes. These machines are known as the Royal Gift, donated to the HMAT personally by
       <a href="/wiki/King" title="King">
        King
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boris_III" title="Boris III">
        Boris III
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1937, during the traditional military parade of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._George%27s_Day#Orthodox_countries" title="St. George's Day">
        St. George's Day
       </a>
       (National Day of Bravery and of the patron-saint of the Bulgarian Armed Forces), military aircraft officially debuted as a part of the armed forces after a nearly two-decade hiatus. A month later Boris III himself presented the Bulgarian air regiments with their new combat flags at an official ceremony at Vrazhdebna Airfield.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1937 14
       <a href="/wiki/PZL_P.24" title="PZL P.24">
        PZL P.24
       </a>
       B fighters and 12
       <a href="/wiki/PZL.43" title="PZL.43">
        PZL.43
       </a>
       A light bombers were ordered from Poland, with deliveries starting later that year, while in 1938, orders were placed for 42 more PZL.43B light bombers and 12 PZL.24F fighters, which differed from the earlier aircraft in having more powerful engines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AE39_p63_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AE39_p63-6">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">
        Third Reich
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Czechoslovakia" title="German occupation of Czechoslovakia">
        occupied
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovakia
       </a>
       in 1938, the Czechoslovak air force was broken up. Bulgaria used the opportunity to acquire large numbers of relatively modern ex-Czech aircraft from the Germans at a bargain price. Bulgaria purchased 78
       <a href="/wiki/Avia_B-534" title="Avia B-534">
        Avia B-534
       </a>
       biplane fighters, 32 Avia B.71 bombers (a license version of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_SB" title="Tupolev SB">
        Soviet SB
       </a>
       bomber), 12
       <a href="/wiki/Bloch_MB.200" title="Bloch MB.200">
        Bloch MB.200
       </a>
       bombers, 62
       <a href="/wiki/Letov_%C5%A0-28" title="Letov Š-28">
        Letov Š-328
       </a>
       reconnaissance aircraft and 28
       <a href="/wiki/Avia_B.122" title="Avia B.122">
        Avia Bs.122
       </a>
       trainers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AE39_p64-5_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AE39_p64-5-7">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Deliveries of the second batch of Polish orders started in early 1939, with 33 PZL.43Bs and 8 PZL.11Fs delivered before the
       <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">
        German invasion of Poland
       </a>
       stopped deliveries (although two more PZL.43Bs were delivered by the Germans later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AE39_p66_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AE39_p66-8">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In less than 3 years the Air Force inventory had grown up to 478 aircraft of which 135 were of Bulgarian construction.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="World_War_II_.281939.E2.80.931945.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_(1939–1945)">
        World War II (1939–1945)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: World War II (1939–1945)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1941-1944).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281941-1944%29.svg/160px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281941-1944%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281941-1944%29.svg/240px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281941-1944%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281941-1944%29.svg/320px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281941-1944%29.svg.png 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1941-1944).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Insignia from 1941 to 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       At the beginning of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , the combat air fleet comprised 374 machines in various roles. In addition orders were placed for 10
       <a href="/wiki/Messerschmitt_Bf_109" title="Messerschmitt Bf 109">
        Messerschmitt Bf 109E-4
       </a>
       fighters, 11
       <a href="/wiki/Dornier_Do_17" title="Dornier Do 17">
        Dornier Do 17
       </a>
       M/P bombers, 6
       <a href="/wiki/Messerschmitt_Bf_108" title="Messerschmitt Bf 108">
        Messerschmitt Bf 108
       </a>
       light liaison and utility aircraft, 24
       <a href="/wiki/Arado_Ar_96" title="Arado Ar 96">
        Arado Ar 96
       </a>
       B-2
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apmar72_p94_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-apmar72_p94-9">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 14
       <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCcker_B%C3%BC_131" title="Bücker Bü 131">
        Bücker-Bestmann Bü 131
       </a>
       trainers.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Air Force order of battle comprised the 1st, 2nd, 3rd and 4th Army Aviation Orlyaks (Army Air Groups or air regiments), each attached to the correspondingly-numbered field army. Each orlyak had a fighter, a line bomber and two reconnaissance yatos (Squadrons). There was also an Independent Aviation corps, which combined the 5th Bomber and 6th Fighter Regiments. The training units consisted of the "Junker" School Orlyak at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vrazhdebna" title="Vrazhdebna">
        Vrazhdebna
       </a>
       airfield, the 2nd Training Orlyak at Telish airfield (called the Blind Flying Training School) and the 3rd Training Orlyak at
       <a href="/wiki/Stara_Zagora" title="Stara Zagora">
        Stara Zagora
       </a>
       airfield. In 1940, the Bulgarian aviation industry provided the HMAT with 42 DAR-9, 45 KB-5 aircraft and the serial production of the
       <a href="/wiki/Caproni_Ca.309" title="Caproni Ca.309">
        KB-6
       </a>
       – Bulgaria's first twin-engined aircraft was scheduled to commence. At year's end the Air Force had 595 aircraft (258 combat) and 10 287 personnel.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1263" data-file-width="1593" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png/220px-Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png/330px-Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png/440px-Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarien_Air_Forces_August_1944.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Disposition of Bulgarian Air Force in August 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria" title="Kingdom of Bulgaria">
        Kingdom of Bulgaria
       </a>
       signed the
       <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Pact" title="Tripartite Pact">
        Tripartite Pact
       </a>
       , becoming a formal ally of Germany.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apmar72_p94_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-apmar72_p94-9">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under the treaty, Bulgaria allowed the use of its territory as a staging point for the invasion of Yugoslavia and Greece and some minor logistical support.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite the impressive inventory, Bulgaria's fighter force at the time consisted of 91 machines, with just 10 of them being of the modern Bf 109E-4 type. Further 11 were of the outdated PZL.24B; the remaining numbers were of the Avia B.534 biplane types. The ground-based air defenses were made up of only 8 88 mm (3.5 in) and 6 20 mm (0.79 in) AA guns. To help its new ally the 12th Army of the Wehrmacht offered support with its air and air defense assets and 8 Freya-type radars dispersed throughout the country. A dispersed observation and reporting system was gradually developed.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The first air strike against Bulgarian targets was carried out by 4
       <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">
        Yugoslav
       </a>
       Dornier Do.17Kb-1 on 6 April 1941 on the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Kyustendil" title="Kyustendil">
        Kyustendil
       </a>
       and its railway station killing 47 and injuring 95, mostly civilians.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The air strikes intensified in the following days; British
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">
        Royal Air Force
       </a>
       units based in
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greece
       </a>
       participated in the
       <a href="/wiki/Offensive_(military)" title="Offensive (military)">
        attacks
       </a>
       as well. At the end of April, the 2nd and 5th
       <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">
        Bulgarian
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">
        armies
       </a>
       occupied
       <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">
        Greek
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">
        Yugoslav
       </a>
       territories according to an agreement with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">
        Third Reich
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       As a part of the joint armed forces' effort on June 26, 1941 6 Avia B.71 and 9 Dornier Do 17M bombers were transferred to the Badem Chiflik airfield near
       <a href="/wiki/Kavala" title="Kavala">
        Kavala
       </a>
       (in modern Greece). They were tasked with ASW patrols and air support for Italian shipping over the adjacent area of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">
        Aegean Sea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In addition 9 Letov Š.328s based in Badem Chiflik provided the ground troops with air reconnaissance. At the Black Sea shores the "Galata" Fighter Orlyak was established at
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NAS_Chaika&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NAS Chaika (page does not exist)">
        NAS Chaika
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">
        Varna
       </a>
       , with the 10 Bf 109E-4s and 6 Avia B.534s. The S.328s were also used for ASW patrols over the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">
        Black Sea
       </a>
       , flying out of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sarafovo" title="Sarafovo">
        Sarafovo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Balchik" title="Balchik">
        Balchik
       </a>
       airfields. At the end of 1941 the inventory of His Majesty's Air Troops consisted of 609 aircraft of 40 different types.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 22 June 1941,
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">
        Germany invaded the Soviet Union
       </a>
       , but Bulgaria refused to take part, although it did declare war with Great Britain and the United States of America in December 1941. Bulgaria's inaction against the Soviet Union meant that supplies of German aircraft slowed to a trickle, with only four aircraft delivered from January to September 1942.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apap72_p141_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-apap72_p141-10">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The war declared by the Kingdom of Bulgaria against the USA and Great Britain was a tragedy for the little country. On August 1, 1943, an enormous armada of about 700 American B-24 Liberator bombers flew over several Balkan countries. This mission was
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tidal_Wave" title="Operation Tidal Wave">
        Operation Tidal Wave
       </a>
       – a long time prepared US raid of WW2. Its target was "the taproot of German might" – the giant oil refineries at Ploesti,Rumania. Sofia city and other Bulgarian towns and villages were hit by following air strikes in late 1943 and in 1944. So 187 inhabited places were attacked, 45,000 destructive and incendiary bombs were dropped, there were about 2,000 casualties, and about 4700 wounded.There were 12,000 damaged or ruined buildings and the total losses were estimated at nearly 24 billion dollars. For the citizens of Sofia the "Black" days were 14 and 24 November, 10 and 20 December 1943, and 10 January and 16, 24, 30 March and 17 April 1944 when large formations of B-17 and B-24 bombers ruined some parts of the capital city including the central part.
      </p>
      <p>
       In total, about 23,000 enemy sorties were registered over Bulgaria in the years 1943–1944. Bulgarian pilots fought an enemy outnumbering them by 10 to 50 times. Some of the best pilots were Lieutenant Stoyan Stoyanov, Captain Chudomir Toplodolsky, and Lieutenants Bochev, Cvetkov, and Damev. 19 Bulgarian pilots died in this war against the Allies. The Allies lost 60 planes, shot down by Bulgarian fighters and about 430 airmen, 325 of which were taken as POWs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reestablishment_under_the_Communist_government">
        Reestablishment under the Communist government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Reestablishment under the Communist government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1944-1946).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281944-1946%29.svg/160px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281944-1946%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281944-1946%29.svg/240px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281944-1946%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281944-1946%29.svg/320px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281944-1946%29.svg.png 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1944-1946).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Insignia from 1945 to 1948
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1946-1992).svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1660" data-file-width="1750" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281946-1992%29.svg/160px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281946-1992%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281946-1992%29.svg/240px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281946-1992%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281946-1992%29.svg/320px-Roundel_of_Bulgaria_%281946-1992%29.svg.png 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roundel_of_Bulgaria_(1946-1992).svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Insignia from 1949 to 1992
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Bulgarian Air Force, along with other branches of the military, adopted the doctrine of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_deep_battle" title="Soviet deep battle">
        Soviet deep battle
       </a>
       in its Cold War development. The force expanded rapidly with deliveries of different types of combat aircraft. The first shipments of Soviet equipment arrived immediately after the end of World War II, mostly consisting of propeller-driven aircraft, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-2" title="Ilyushin Il-2">
        Ilyushin Il-2
       </a>
       (120 Il-2 and 10 Il-2U), the
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-10" title="Ilyushin Il-10">
        Ilyushin Il-10
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Tupolev_Tu-2" title="Tupolev Tu-2">
        Tupolev Tu-2
       </a>
       . By 1954, these types were withdrawn from service, as the
       <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">
        Korean War
       </a>
       marked the beginning of the jet fighter era. In 1955 a new wave of deliveries began, which included
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-15" title="MiG-15">
        MiG-15
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-17" title="MiG-17">
        MiG-17
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-19" title="MiG-19">
        MiG-19
       </a>
       fighters and
       <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin_Il-28" title="Ilyushin Il-28">
        Ilyushin Il-28
       </a>
       bombers, as well as the first helicopters (
       <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-1" title="Mil Mi-1">
        Mil Mi-1
       </a>
       ). These aircraft were withdrawn in the 1970s, when the last wave of modernization began.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 1979 the
       <a href="/wiki/Mil_Moscow_Helicopter_Plant" title="Mil Moscow Helicopter Plant">
        Mil
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mi-24_Hind" title="Mi-24 Hind">
        Mi-24 Hind
       </a>
       entered service through a significant re-equipment program and a boost to rotary power to the BVVS. The
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi" title="Sukhoi">
        Sukhoi
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-25_Frogfoot" title="Su-25 Frogfoot">
        Su-25 Frogfoot
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi" title="Sukhoi">
        Sukhoi
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-22" title="Su-22">
        Su-22
       </a>
       entered service in 1988 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">
        strike
       </a>
       /
       <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance" title="Reconnaissance">
        reconnaissance
       </a>
       role. 40 Su-25K/KUBs were delivered and 21 Su-22M4/UM-3s were delivered. In total, by 1989 the Bulgarian Air Force had received and operated:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        224
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-21" title="MiG-21">
         MiG-21
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        90
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-23" title="MiG-23">
         MiG-23
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        4
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-25" title="MiG-25">
         MiG-25
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        22
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">
         MiG-29
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        23
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-22" title="Su-22">
         Su-22
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        35
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-25" title="Su-25">
         Su-25
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        54
        <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-24" title="Mil Mi-24">
         Mil Mi-24
        </a>
        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
         [
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
            citation needed
           </span>
          </a>
         </i>
         ]
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span id="After_the_Cold_War_.281989.E2.80.932004.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_Cold_War_(1989–2004)">
        After the Cold War (1989–2004)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: After the Cold War (1989–2004)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG/220px-Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG/330px-Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG/440px-Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uzundzhovo_memorial_complex.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Former MiG-21 at the Uzundzhovo memorial complex.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1993 the air regiments in Bezmer and Sadovo were experimentally transformed into "air bases" with the merger of the air regiments with the aviation-technical and airfield service battalions, that were independent from them. Around 1995 – 1996 all the air regiments were transformed into air bases (brigade equivalents) and two main commands were formed – Air Defence Command (Командване за противовъздушна отбрана), merging the two air defence divisions and the Tactical Aviation Command (Командване Тактическа Авиация), by reorganisation of the
       <a href="/wiki/10th_Composite_Aviation_Corps" title="10th Composite Aviation Corps">
        10th Composite Aviation Corps
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       called and including into it the newly transformed into air bases training regiments in Shtraklevo and Kamenets. The regiment in Dolna Mitropoliya was disbanded.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the end of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_war" title="Cold war">
        Cold war
       </a>
       Bulgaria's air force is limited to 226 aircraft. A large number of early MiG-21 variants were withdrawn from service and were cut for scrap, and armament from the trainers for the MiG-21 and MiG-23 was removed. In 1998 four air bases were closed down: Gabrovnitsa, Balchick,
       <a href="/wiki/Uzundzhovo" title="Uzundzhovo">
        Uzundzhovo
       </a>
       and Shtraklevo. Then in 2000 the Stara Zagora (operating Mi-24s) air force base was closed. Then in 2001 three more bases were closed down: Dobrich, Ravnets and Cheshnegirovo. In 2003 Dobroslavtsi was closed down and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-23" title="MiG-23">
        MiG-23s
       </a>
       were withdrawn from service, because it is more expensive to run than the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-21" title="MiG-21">
        MiG-21
       </a>
       . In February 2004 the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-22" title="Su-22">
        Su-22s
       </a>
       , which were stationed first in Dobrich then in Bezmer, were withdrawn.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_times">
        Modern times
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

        </a>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
