         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="950" data-file-width="1264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bulgarian_cougar_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Bulgarian_cougar_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bulgarian_cougar_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Bulgarian_cougar_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Bulgarian_cougar_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Bulgarian_cougar_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_cougar_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bulgarian Eurocopter AS532 Cougar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Since the early 2000s, Bulgaria has been trying actively to restructure its armed forces as a whole and a lot of attention has been placed on keeping the aging Russian aircraft operational. Currently the attack and defence branches of the Bulgarian air force are composed of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-21" title="MiG-21">
        MiG-21s
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">
        MiG-29s
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       About 16
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">
        MiG-29
       </a>
       fighters have been modernized in order to meet
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       standards. In January 2011 the Bulgarian MoD issued a Request for Information (RFI) regarding the acquisition of 8 multi-role fighters.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The main competitors are expected to be the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">
        Eurofighter Typhoon
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dassault" title="Dassault">
        Dassault
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rafale" title="Rafale">
        Rafale
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saab_Group" title="Saab Group">
        Saab
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JAS_39_Gripen" title="JAS 39 Gripen">
        JAS 39 Gripen
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan" title="Mikoyan">
        Mikoyan
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">
        MiG-29
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-35" title="MiG-35">
        MiG-35
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">
        Lockheed Martin
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-16" title="F-16">
        F-16
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">
        Boeing
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F/A-18_Super_Hornet" title="F/A-18 Super Hornet">
        F/A-18 Super Hornet
       </a>
       . On March 9, 2011 the Swedish Government submitted its response to the RFI containing 8 new Gripen C/D fighters. The Bulgarian MoD has extended the time limit for submittal of responses by two months due to the lack of responses from the other competitors.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Bulgaria's government has announced the
       <a href="/wiki/Saab_Group" title="Saab Group">
        Saab
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JAS_39_Gripen" title="JAS 39 Gripen">
        JAS 39 Gripen
       </a>
       as the preferred candidate in the country’s new combat aircraft competition. Sofia late last year issued a request for proposals for the purchase of eight multirole fighters, to be delivered by 2020.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, a new government postponed plans of acquiring new aircraft in May 2017.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2006 the Bulgarian government signed a contract with
       <a href="/wiki/Alenia_Aeronautica" title="Alenia Aeronautica">
        Alenia Aeronautica
       </a>
       for the delivery of five
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-27J_Spartan" title="C-27J Spartan">
        C-27J Spartan
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Military_transport_aircraft" title="Military transport aircraft">
        transport aircraft
       </a>
       in order to replace the older Soviet
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/An-24" title="An-24">
        An-24
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/An-26" title="An-26">
        An-26
       </a>
       . The first Spartan arrived in 2007. Now, the contract has changed to the delivery of only 3 planes and final plane arrived on 31 March 2011.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Modern European transport
       <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">
        helicopters
       </a>
       were ordered and purchased in 2005 and until now 12
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocopter_Cougar" title="Eurocopter Cougar">
        Eurocopter Cougar
       </a>
       helicopters (8 transport and 4
       <a href="/wiki/Combat_search_and_rescue" title="Combat search and rescue">
        CSAR
       </a>
       ) have arrived. For the Navy 3
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocopter_Panther" title="Eurocopter Panther">
        Eurocopter Panther
       </a>
       were ordered and have been delivered.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="847" data-file-width="1280" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg/220px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg/330px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg/440px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Air_Force_Aero_L-39ZA_Albatros_Lofting-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">

         L-39ZA Albatros
        </div>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1280" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg/220px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg/330px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg/440px-Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Air_Force_Pilatus_PC-9M_Lofting-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Pilatus PC-9M
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Mi24.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="302" data-file-width="805" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bulgarian_Mi24.png/220px-Bulgarian_Mi24.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bulgarian_Mi24.png/330px-Bulgarian_Mi24.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bulgarian_Mi24.png/440px-Bulgarian_Mi24.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_Mi24.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bulgarian Mi-24
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Branches of the air force include:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Fighter aviation
       </li>
       <li>
        Fighter-bomber aviation
       </li>
       <li>
        Ground attack aviation
       </li>
       <li>
        Tactical reconnaissance aviation
       </li>
       <li>
        Transport aviation
       </li>
       <li>
        Missile aid defense troops
       </li>
       <li>
        Radio-technical troops
       </li>
       <li>
        Communications troops
       </li>
       <li>
        Logistics and medical troops.
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       Bulgaria is planning to reinforce the international forces in
       <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">
        Afghanistan
       </a>
       by sending two Mil Mi-17 transport helicopters to the country. As a result, a special fund was created that will provide money for the renovation of older Soviet-made equipment, which could then be used in Afghanistan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_Inventory">
        Aircraft Inventory
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Aircraft Inventory">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_Bulgarian_military_aircraft" title="List of active Bulgarian military aircraft">
        List of active Bulgarian military aircraft
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="2049" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG/220px-Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG/330px-Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG/440px-Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bell_206_bulgaria_02.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bulgarian Bell-206
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       With the exception of the Navy's small helicopter fleet, the Air Force is responsible for all military aircraft in Bulgaria. The Air Force's inventory numbers around 90 aircraft, including 47 combat jets, but only the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MiG-29" title="MiG-29">
        MiG-29s
       </a>
       , about a dozen
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-25" title="Su-25">
        Su-25s
       </a>
       are flight worthy. The
       <a href="/wiki/Aero_L-39_Albatros" title="Aero L-39 Albatros">
        L-39ZA
       </a>
       is only used for training. The condition of some of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Su-25" title="Su-25">
        Su-25
       </a>
       Ks is bad, but the Air Force is capable of overhauling and repairing them.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       There are around 23–30 helicopters operated by the Bulgarian Air Force at the moment, including just one
       <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-24" title="Mil Mi-24">
        Mil Mi-24
       </a>
       attack helicopter. Aircraft of Western origin have only begun to enter the fleet, numbering 27 of the total in service.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Bulgaria signed a deal with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocopter" title="Eurocopter">
        Eurocopter
       </a>
       worth 358 million euros for purchase of 12 AS 532
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocopter_Cougar" title="Eurocopter Cougar">
        Eurocopter Cougar
       </a>
       (4 of which are modified for
       <a href="/wiki/Combat_search_and_rescue" title="Combat search and rescue">
        CSAR
       </a>
       ) and 2
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocopter_Panther" title="Eurocopter Panther">
        Eurocopter Panther
       </a>
       AS 565. The country also agreed to the purchase of 5
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C27J" title="C27J">
        C27J
       </a>
       transports with
       <a href="/wiki/Alenia_Aeronautica" title="Alenia Aeronautica">
        Alenia
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italy
       </a>
       , a deal worth some 210 million €. At the end, only 3 Spartan had been delivered.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The BuAf plans to retire most of its
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet
       </a>
       -era aircraft, keeping only the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikoyan-Gurevich_MiG-29" title="Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-29">
        Mikoyan-Gurevich MiG-29
       </a>
       "Fulcrum" fleet which was modernized only recently, as well as its
       <a href="/wiki/Mil_Mi-24" title="Mil Mi-24">
        Mil Mi-24
       </a>
       gunships and
       <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_Su-25" title="Sukhoi Su-25">
        Sukhoi Su-25s
       </a>
       . The MiG-21s in service were scheduled to be replaced with possible American or European aircraft.
      </p>
      <p>
       On November 11, 2016, the Bulgarian government signed a 21.8-million euro contract for 10 MiG-29 engines (four new and six repaired), with the first pair scheduled to arrive by April 2017. The deal would eventually bring the number of active service MiG-29 aircraft from 9 to 14, as Bulgaria also announced it was looking to overhaul the fleet and buy eight new or second-hand fighter jets during the coming year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_facilities">
        Notable facilities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notable facilities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg/220px-Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg/330px-Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg/440px-Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulgarian_sa-10_launcher.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bulgarian S300P
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BulgarianMig23BN.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="641" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/BulgarianMig23BN.png/220px-BulgarianMig23BN.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/BulgarianMig23BN.png/330px-BulgarianMig23BN.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/BulgarianMig23BN.png/440px-BulgarianMig23BN.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BulgarianMig23BN.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Bulgarian Mig 23BN in
         <a href="/wiki/Cheshnegirovo_Air_Base" title="Cheshnegirovo Air Base">
          Cheshnegirovo Air Base
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Facilities_of_the_Bulgarian_Air_Force" title="Facilities of the Bulgarian Air Force">
        Facilities of the Bulgarian Air Force
       </a>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        1st Fighter Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Dobroslavtsi_Air_Base" title="Dobroslavtsi Air Base">
         Dobroslavtsi Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        2nd Fighter Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Gabrovnitsa_Air_Base" title="Gabrovnitsa Air Base">
         Gabrovnitsa Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        3rd Fighter Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Graf_Ignatievo_Air_Base" title="Graf Ignatievo Air Base">
         Graf Ignatievo Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        5th Fighter Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Ravnets_Air_Base" title="Ravnets Air Base">
         Ravnets Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        6th Fighter Air Base –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balchik_Air_Base" title="Balchik Air Base">
         Balchik Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        11th Training Air Base –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shtraklevo_Air_Base" title="Shtraklevo Air Base">
         Shtraklevo Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        12th Training Air Base – Kamenets (now transferred to
        <a href="/wiki/Dolna_Mitropoliya" title="Dolna Mitropoliya">
         Dolna Mitropoliya
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        16th Transport Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Vrazhdebna_Air_Base" title="Vrazhdebna Air Base">
         Vrazhdebna Air Base
        </a>
        (military area of
        <a href="/wiki/Sofia_Airport" title="Sofia Airport">
         Sofia Airport
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        21st Fighter-Bomber Air Base –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uzundzhovo_Air_Base" title="Uzundzhovo Air Base">
         Uzundzhovo Air Base
        </a>
        (formerly 4th FAB)
       </li>
       <li>
        22nd Ground Attack Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Bezmer_Air_Base" title="Bezmer Air Base">
         Bezmer Air Base
        </a>
        (becoming a joint Bulgarian-American training facility)
       </li>
       <li>
        23rd Attack Helicopters Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Stara_Zagora_Air_Base" title="Stara Zagora Air Base">
         Stara Zagora Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        24th Helicopter Air Base –
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krumovo_Air_Base" title="Krumovo Air Base">
         Krumovo Air Base
        </a>
        (military area of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plovdiv_International_Airport" title="Plovdiv International Airport">
         Plovdiv Airport
        </a>
        )
       </li>
       <li>
        25th Fighter-Bomber Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Cheshnegirovo_Air_Base" title="Cheshnegirovo Air Base">
         Cheshnegirovo Air Base
        </a>
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Sadovo" title="Sadovo">
         Sadovo
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        26th Reconnaissance Air Base –
        <a href="/wiki/Dobrich_Air_Base" title="Dobrich Air Base">
         Dobrich Air Base
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bozhurishte_Airfield&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bozhurishte Airfield (page does not exist)">
         Bozhurishte Airfield
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        The city of
        <a href="/wiki/Plovdiv" title="Plovdiv">
         Plovdiv
        </a>
        used to house the headquarters of the Tactical Aviation Command and is still a place of significance as it houses a number of logistical and operational support units of the Bulgarian Air Force.
       </li>
       <li>
        The city of
        <a href="/wiki/Burgas" title="Burgas">
         Burgas
        </a>
        is the place around which the 3rd Missile Air Defence Brigade of the Bulgarian Air Force is deployed.
       </li>
       <li>
        63rd Independent Maritime Helicopter Air Base at
        <a href="/wiki/Varna" title="Varna">
         Varna
        </a>
        –
        <a href="/wiki/Chayka_Naval_Air_Base" title="Chayka Naval Air Base">
         Chayka Naval Air Base
        </a>
        , which houses the Independent Maritime Helicopter Squadron.
       </li>
      </ul>

        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulgarian_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-4">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-4">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           The Bulgarian word "yato" means a "flock of birds" and was the Bulgarian equivalent of an air force squadron at the time
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-5">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-5">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           The Bulgarian word "orlyak" used here means a "Air Group"
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>
